Figure 2.21 Number of total bits as a function of image size and number of bits used to represent the image pixels.

MATLAB Function used to create plot:

function b = bytesvssize(N, k)
% Implements the equation b = N^2 * k where N is image size and k is the
% number of bits in each pixel (when k = 1 the image is binary and when k =
% 8 the image has 256 intensity levels). b is the total number of bits in
% the image as a function of N and k.
K = 1:k;
sz = 1:N;
b(1:k, 1:numel(sz))=0;
for I = 1:k
    b(I,1:numel(sz)) = K(I)*(sz(1:numel(sz)).^2)/8;
end
figure, plot(sz,b(1,:))
hold on
for I = 2:k
    plot(sz,b(I,:))
    hold on
end

Figure 2.23 Reducing Resolution. (Redone from 3rd edition)
>> f = imread('Fig0223(a)(chronometer 2136x2140  2pt3 inch 930 dpi).tif');
>> % Reduce to 300 dpi (size 689x690) using nearest neighbor interpolation.
>> gnn = imresize(f, [689 690], 'nearest');
>> % Zoom back to original size.
>> fr300dpi = imresize(gnn, size(f), 'nearest');
>> % Now do 150 dpi (size 345x345)
>> gnn = imresize(f, [345 345], 'nearest');
>> % Zoom back to original size.
>> fr150dpi = imresize(gnn, size(f), 'nearest');
>> % Now do 72 dpi (size 165x166)
>> gnn = imresize(f, [165 166], 'nearest');
>> % Zoom back to original size.
>> fr72dpi = imresize(gnn, size(f), 'nearest');
>> figure, imshow(f)
>> figure, imshow(fr300dpi)
>> figure, imshow(fr150dpi)
>> figure, imshow(fr72dpi)
>> % Save results with the same size (resolution) as the original image.
>> imwrite(fr300dpi, 'Fig0223(b)(chronometer 689x690 2pt3 inch 300 dpi).tif','compression','none','resolution',930)
>> imwrite(fr150dpi, 'Fig0223(c)(chronometer 345x345 2pt3 inch 150 dpi).tif','compression','none','resolution',930)
>> imwrite(fr72dpi, 'Fig0223(d)(chronometer 165x166 2pt3 inch 72 dpi).tif','compression','none','resolution',930)

Figure 2.24 (False Countouring).  

[Note: The functions im2bitplanes and bitplanes2im used here are the ones I wrote for Richard Blake's project. 

>> f256 = imread('drip-bottle.tif'); 
>> % Get all the bit planes.
>> B = im2bitplanes(f256, 8); 
>> % Reduce image to 7 bits (i.e., use the 7 highest order bit planes)
>> f128 = bitplanes2im(B, [2 3 4 5 6 7 8]);
>> % Repeat down to 2 bits.
>> f64 = bitplanes2im(B, [3 4 5 6 7 8]);
>> f32 = bitplanes2im(B, [4 5 6 7 8]);
>> f16 = bitplanes2im(B, [5 6 7 8]);
>> f8 = bitplanes2im(B, [6 7 8]);
>> f4 = bitplanes2im(B, [7 8]);
>> f2 = bitplanes2im(B, [8]); % Creating a binary image this way only uses the lower 7 bits, which produces a gray
                              % and black image. Changed it manually in photoshop so that it would be black & white.

>> f128 = im2uint8(f128);
>> f64 = im2uint8(f64);
>> f32 = im2uint8(f32);
>> f16 = im2uint8(f16);
>> f8 = im2uint8(f8);
>> f4 = im2uint8(f4);
>> f2 = im2uint8(f2);


>> figure, imshow(f256)
>> figure, imshow(f128)
>> figure, imshow(f64)
>> figure, imshow(f32)
>> figure, imshow(f16)
>> figure, imshow(f8)
>> figure, imshow(f4)
>> figure, imshow(f2)

>> % Write results to disk
>> imwrite(f256, 'Fig0221(a)(original 256 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f128, 'Fig0221(b)(128 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f64, 'Fig0221(c)(64 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f32, 'Fig0221(d)(32 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f16, 'Fig0221(e)(16 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f8, 'Fig0221(f)(8 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f4, 'Fig0221(g)(4 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)
>> imwrite(f2, 'Fig0221(h)(2 levels).tif','compression','none','resolution',783)

MATERIAL FOR NEW PROBLEM:  (a) The range of values in the original image is [0 255].  However, the range of values in the binary image is only [0 128]. Explain why this is so.  [Answer:  Using only the 8th bit plane, which is multiplied by 2^(k - 1), which is 127. (b) In general, what can you say about the range of pixel values of the 4, 8, 16, 32, 64, and 128-level images. Ans: the 0's will remain 0's, but the higher values will decrease in general. (Explain why the 0s remain 0s') If can't use this problem here, use it in Chapter 3 when talk about bit planes.

MATERIAL FOR NEW PROBLEM: Mention that an image can be decomposed into bit planes.  Then ask questions about it. (Bit planes are introduced in Chapter 3, so look at that section for ideas.)

MATERIAL FOR NEW PROJECT: Write a MATLAB function to decrease the number of levels in an image. You may assume that the images are 8 bits.  Do using intensity transformation functions and also by bit-plane decomposition.

Figure 2.27 Reducing Resolution and Zooming Back. 

>> f = imread('Fig0224(original)(chronometer 2136x2140  1pt9 inch 1125 dpi).tif');
>> % Reduce images to 72 dpi (down to size 165x166 from 2136x2140 and then
>> % Zoom back to original size using nearest neighbor, bilinear, and bicubic
>> % interpolation.
>> g72nn = imresize(f,[165 166],'nearest');
>> f72zoomnn = imresize(g72nn, size(f),'nearest');
>> g72bl = imresize(f,[165 166],'bilinear');
>> f72zoombl = imresize(g72bl, size(f),'bilinear');
>> g72bc = imresize(f,[165 166],'bicubic');
>> f72zoombc = imresize(g72bc, size(f),'bicubic');

>> % Show results
>> figure, imshow(f72zoomnn)
>> figure, imshow(f72zoombl)
>> figure, imshow(f72zoombc)

>> % Save results
>> imwrite(f72zoomnn, 'Fig0227(a)(down to 72 dpi and zoomed back using nn interp).tif','compression','none','resolution',1125)
>> imwrite(f72zoombl, 'Fig0227(b)(down to 72 dpi and zoomed back using bl interp).tif','compression','none','resolution',1125)
>> imwrite(f72zoombc, 'Fig0227(c)(down to 72 dpi and zoomed back using bc interp).tif','compression','none','resolution',1125)

%% DIDN'T USE THE 150 DPI RESULTS. THEY ARE CONFUSING BECAUSE THERE'S NOT MUCH CHANGE.

>> % Now repeat using reduction to 150 dpi (344x345) and returning to the original size
>> g150nn = imresize(f,[344 345],'nearest');
>> f150zoomnn = imresize(g150nn, size(f),'nearest');
>> g150bl = imresize(f,[344 345],'bilinear');
>> f150zoombl = imresize(g150bl, size(f),'bilinear');
>> g150bc = imresize(f,[344 345],'bicubic');
>> f150zoombc = imresize(g150bc, size(f),'bicubic');

>> figure, imshow(f150zoomnn)
>> figure, imshow(f150zoombl)
>> figure, imshow(f150zoombc)

>> imwrite(f150zoomnn, 'Fig0227(d)(down to 150 dpi and zoomed back using nn interp).tif','compression','none','resolution',1125)
>> imwrite(f150zoombl, 'Fig0227(e)(down to 150 dpi and zoomed back using bl interp).tif','compression','none','resolution',1125)
>> imwrite(f150zoombc, 'Fig0227(f)(down to 150 dpi and zoomed back using bc interp).tif','compression','none','resolution',1125)

Figure 2.29 Noise reduction by image averaging {Redone from 3rd edition}

*** DOING IT WITH THE FULL IMAGE (Sombrero Galaxy)

>> forig = imread('sombrero_galaxy (original).tif'); % Original full image.
>> forig_noisy = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 1, 'gaussian', 0, 64)); % Sample noisy full image.
>> fav10 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 10, 'gaussian', 0, 64));
>> fav50 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 50, 'gaussian', 0, 64));
>> fav100 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 100, 'gaussian', 0, 64));
>> fav500 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 500, 'gaussian', 0, 64));
>> fav1000 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 1000, 'gaussian', 0, 64));

% Display Results
>> figure, imshow(forig_noisy)
>> figure, imshow(fav10)
>> figure, imshow(fav50)
>> figure, imshow(fav100)
>> figure, imshow(fav500)
>> figure, imshow(fav1000)

imwrite(forig_noisy,'Fig0229(a)(noisy original image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1111)
imwrite(fav10,'Fig0229(b)(average 10 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1111)
imwrite(fav50,'Fig0229(c)(average of 50 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1111)
imwrite(fav100,'Fig0229(d)(average of 100 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1111)
imwrite(fav500,'Fig0229(e)(average of 500 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1111)
imwrite(fav1000,'Fig0229(f)(average of 1000 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1111)

>> fQ100= intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(fQ, 100, 'gaussian', 0, 64)) ;

>> % Generate and add 1000 noisy copies of the full image. %
>> forig = imread('sombrero_galaxy.tif'); % Original full image.
>> forig0 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 1, 'gaussian', 0, 64)); % Sample noisy full image.
>> % Average 1000 noisy images
>> forig1000 = intScaling4e(averaging4noisereduction(forig, 1000, 'gaussian', 0, 64));

% Show results
figure, imshow(forig0)
figure, imshow(fQ0)
figure, imshow(fQ5)
figure, imshow(fQ10)
figure, imshow(fQ50)
figure, imshow(fQ100)
figure, imshow(fQ500)
figure, imshow(fQ1000)
figure, imshow(forig1000)

imwrite(forig0,'Fig0228(a)(noisy original image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1176)
imwrite(fQ0,'Fig0228(b)(noisy quadrant image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(fQ5,'Fig0228(c)(noisy quadrant image average of 5 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(fQ10,'Fig0228(d)(noisy quadrant image average of 10 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(fQ50,'Fig0228(e)(noisy quadrant image average of 50 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(fQ100,'Fig0228(f)(noisy quadrant image average of 100 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(fQ500,'Fig0228(g)(noisy quadrant image average of 500 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(fQ1000,'Fig0228(h)(noisy quadrant image average of 1000 images).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 588)
imwrite(forig1000,'Fig0228(i)(average of 1000 noisy samples of original image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 1176)

NOTES When discussing results.
 
1) Values of noisy images will exceed 255, so all results are shown scaled to [0 255].
2) This is a computer-intensive process, so it typically is done using specialized hardware that can keep up with the data thoughput coming in.
3) Note increase in visibilty if small objects (stars), especially in the light areas of the image, and note the increase in contrast.
4) If haven't done so already, make a problem to show that the sum of noisy images can be done recursively.

Figure 2.31 Differences between original chronometer (930 dpi and 300, 150, and 72 dpi versions from Fig. 2.23) 

% Do Using MATLAB's imsubtract function and see if the results are the same.

>> forig = imread('Fig0223(a)(chronometer 2136x2140  2pt3 inch 930 dpi).tif');
>> f300 = imread('Fig0223(b)(chronometer 689x690 2pt3 inch 300 dpi).tif');
>> f150 = imread('Fig0223(c)(chronometer 345x345 2pt3 inch 150 dpi).tif');
>> f72 = imread('Fig0223(d)(chronometer 165x166 2pt3 inch 72 dpi).tif');

>> d300 = imsubtract(forig,f300);
>> d150 = imsubtract(forig, f150);
>> d72 = imsubtract(forig, f72);

>> figure, imshow(d300);
>> figure, imshow(d150);
>> figure, imshow(d72);

>> % All images are of size 2136x2140. Write at 1062 dpi to be 2.0139" and fit 3 across major + minor columns

>> imwrite(d72,'Fig0231(a)(diff between 930 dpi and 72 dpi images).tif', 'compression','none','resolution',1062)
>> imwrite(d150,'Fig0231(b)(diff between 930 dpi and 150 dpi images).tif', 'compression','none','resolution',1062)
>> imwrite(d300,'Fig0231(c)(diff between 930 dpi and 300 dpi images).tif', 'compression','none','resolution',1062)

Figure 2.32 Image subtraction for angiography

>> mask = im2double(imread('Fig0228(a)(angiography_mask_image).tif'));
>> live = im2double(imread('Fig0228(b)(angiography_live_ image).tif'));
>> d = imsubtract(live,mask);
>> d = mat2gray(d);
>> m = mean2(d);
>> g = intrans(d,'stretch',m - .03,10); 
>> figure, imshow(d)
>> figure, imshow(g)
>> imwrite(d,'Fig02EE(c)(difference_image).tif','compression', 'none', 'resolution',300)
>> imwrite(g,'Fig02EE(d)(difference_image_enhanced).tif','compression', 'none', 'resolution',300)

Figure 2.36 Gray-scale set operations on skeleton image.

>> A = im2double(imread('Fig0236(a)(skeleton).tif'));
>> An = 1-A;
>> B = 3*mean2(A)*ones;
>> union = max(A,B);
>> figure, imshow(A)
>> figure,imshow(An)
>> figure, imshow(union)
>> imwrite(An, 'Fig0236(b)(set_complement).tif','compression','none','resolution',500)
>> imwrite(union, 'Fig0236(c)(set_union).tif','compression','none','resolution',500)

*********************************************************************
Figure 2.42  Image Registration

>> f = imread('Fig0237(a)(characters test pattern).tif');
>> % Generate a sheared image that will then be corrected using tie points.
>> shear = [1 .4 0;.05 1 0;0 0 1];
>> tform = maketform('affine',shear);
>> gd = imtransform(f,tform,'bilinear'); % Geometrically distorted image.
>> figure, imshow(f)
>> figure, imshow(gd)
>> %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
>> % Select the tie points using the interactive tool, cpselect.
>> cpselect(gd, f);  % Generates corresponding control points: base_points are for the base (reference  image (f), and input_points are for the input image gd (image to be transformed).
>> base_points
	114.9692  109.4923
  	618.2154   75.7538
  	600.3538  610.9385
  	 75.0923  633.4308
>> input_points
	118.5971  155.0846
  	623.2462  322.6837
  	629.7279  851.9587
  	104.7077  663.9885
>> %%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%% 
>> tform = cp2tform(input_points, base_points,'affine');
>> g = imtransform(gd,tform,'Xdata',[1 size(f,2)], 'YData',[1 size(f,1)]);
>> figure, imshow(g)
>> % Difference image
>> dif = imsubtract(f,g)
>> imwrite(gd,'Fig0242(b)(geometrically distorted).tif','compression','none','resolution',320)
>> imwrite(g,'Fig0242(c)(corrected image).tif','compression','none','resolution',320)
>> imwrite(dif,'Fig0242(d)(difference image).tif','compression','none', 'resolution',320)

Figure 2.45  Astronaut image corrupted by sinusoidal noise.

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0245(astronaut by moon bolder)(hi-res segment of original NASA image).tif'));
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> % generate sinusoidal noise pattern (r), its DFT (R), and its spectrum (S)
>> [r, R, S] = imnoise3(M, N, [25 25], 0.3);
>> % Noisy image.
>> g = f + r; % Save g later (see below) as .mat file (so negative values will be preserved) for posting in web site.
>> % Scale the result.
>> gs = intScaling4e(g); % g has small negative values, so scaled before writing it out.
>> % Compute the spectrum of g to show in book, so that the noise impulses can be explained.
>> G = fftshift(abs(fft2(g)));
>> Glog = intScaling4e(1 + log(G));
>> % Create notch filters. M = 1650 and N = 2000, so the center of the frequency rectangle
>> % is at (M/2) + 1 = 826 and (N/2) + 1 = 1001. Since the specified noise spike is at 
>> % (826 + 25, 1001 + 25) = (851, 1026), specify one filter at the same location. Remember that the conjugates are
>> % generated automatically.  Also, functions imnoise3 and cnotch use different conventions for specifications (they will be fixed to reconcile
>> % in the 3rd edition of DIPUM)
>> H = cnotch('ideal', 'reject', M, N, [851 1025], 2); %% Small ideal filter does much better than gaussian in this case.
>> % Center to show as image.
>> Hc = intScaling4e(fftshift(H)); % Scale for display purposes.
>> %Filter image.
>> gf = intScaling4e(dftfilt(g, H)); % gf has small negative values, so scaled before writing it out.
>> % Display results.
>> imshow(gs)
>> figure, imshow(Glog)
>> figure, imshow(Hc)
>> figure, imshow(gf) 

% Write results to disk.

 %% SAVE g as Fig0240.mat to post in Web site.  That way, positive and negative values are preserved. Make a note that g has poisitive and negative values, so when displayed without [] will not look the same as in the book.  The commnands are save('Fig0240.mat', 'g').  To get it back, type:  load Fig0240  (no single quotes needed)

>> save('Fig0240.mat', 'g')

>> imwrite(gs, 'Fig0240(a)(noisy_astronaut).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870) 
>> imwrite(Glog, 'Fig0240(b)(spectrum).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870) % Note: used Photoshop to magnified impulses
>> imwrite(Hc, 'Fig0240(c)(filter).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870)  % Filter
>> imwrite(gf, 'Fig0240(d)(filtered image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870)


NOTES WHEN DISCUSSING IMAGE:  
1) Amplitude of sinusoidal interference approximately 40% of highest intensity value.
2) Corrupted image has positive and negative values.
3) Mention in (c) that black represents 0 and white represents 1.
4) Border in (c) is not part of the data.

About the original image:  Apollo 17 Extravehicular Activity - 39 Years Ago Today
39 years ago, today, scientist-astronaut Harrison H. Schmitt is photographed standing next to a huge, split lunar boulder during the third Apollo 17 extravehicular activity (EVA) at the Taurus-Littrow landing site. The Lunar Roving Vehicle (LRV), which transported Schmitt and Eugene A. Cernan to this extravehicular station from their Lunar Module (LM), is seen in the background. The mosaic is made from two frames from Apollo 17 

(from: http://www.nasa.gov/multimedia/imagegallery/iotd.html)

Figure 2.49

Line art and a histogram plot of an image. Easy to duplicate in MATLAB.


**************************************************************************
Figure 2.50 GX histograms of various shapes and corresponding central moments.

% Use a Gaussian with high peak to demonstrate that 3rd moment is 0 and 4th moment is high.
% Use a broad Gaussian to show lower value of 4th moment.
% Use a Rayleigh pdf to demonstrate positive 3rd moment.

>> % Gaussian data
>> rg1 = imnoise2('gaussian',1000000,1,20,1);
>> figure, hist(rg1,100); % Use 100 bins in histogram. 
>> % Gaussian data with a higher variance.
>> rg2 = imnoise2('gaussian',1000000,1,20,5); % Note: the 5 is the STANDARD DEVIATION
>> figure, hist(rg2,100)
>> % Rayleigh data
>> rr = imnoise2('rayleigh',1000000,1,1,80); % Select parameters so that horizontal values are approx the same as the other two plots.
>> figure, hist(rr,100)

>> % Commpute the moments (requires Statistocs Toolbox--except for the mean)
>> mg1 = mean(rg1)
>> mg2 = mean(rg2)
>> mg3 = mean(rr)
>> varg1 = moment(rg1,2)
>> varg2 = moment(rg2,2)
>> varrr = moment(rr,2)
>> mu3g1 = moment(rg1,3)
>> mu3g2 = moment(rg2,3)
>> mu3rr = moment(rr,3)
>> mu4g1 = moment(rg1,4)
>> mu4g2 = moment(rg2,4)

Figure 2.53 Gaussian PDF and CDF

>> %PDF
>> z = -20:.001:20;
>> S = 5;
>> m = 0;
>> G =(1/(sqrt(2*pi)*S))*exp((-(z - m).^2)/(2*(S^2)));
>> figure, plot(G)

>> %CDF
>> runningSum = G(1);
>> F(1) = runningSum;
>> for I = 2:numel(G)
>> runningSum = runningSum + G(I);
>> F(I) = runningSum;
>> end
>> figure, plot(F)

>> C = [12 6;6 5];
>> C = [12 -6;-6 5];

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0312(a)(kidney).tif'));
>> rmax = max(f(:));
>> m = 1.35*mean2(f);
>> T1 = piecewisetrans([0 m (m + .1) rmax (rmax + .1) 1],[0 0 1 1 0 0], 256);

>> figure, imshow(g1)
>> m = mean2(f);
>> T2 = piecewisetrans([0 (m - .15) (m - .15 + .05) (m + .15) (m + .15 + .05) 1], [0 (m - .15) 0 0 (m + .15 + .05) 1], 256);

>> figure, imshow(g2)

NOTES FOR FIGURE CAPTION

from:  http://phil.cdc.gov/phil/details.asp?pid=11621

ID#: 11621 
Description: This scanning electron micrograph (SEM) revealed the ventral surface of a Giardia muris trophozoite that had settled atop the mucosal surface of a rat’s intestine. Note the microvilli, which can be seen in the background, as tiny rounded structures that are approximately 0.15 microns in diameter. These microvilli cover the surface of each intestinal epithelial cell. The Giardia’s ventral adhesive disk resembles a suction cup, where overlapping microtubules in the cytoplasm form a number-6-shaped figure. The edge of the suction cup, called the ventrolateral flange, partially encircles the adhesive disk and is absent posteriorly where a ventral pair of flagella emerges from above, dorsal to the disk. Giardia muris has four pairs of flagella that are responsible for the organism’s motility. The adhesive disk facilitates adherence to the intestinal surface.
The protozoan Giardia causes the diarrheal disease called giardiasis. Giardia species exist as free-swimming (by means of flagella) trophozoites, and as egg-shaped cysts. It is the cystic stage, which facilitates the survival of these organisms under harsh environmental conditions. The cyst is considered the infective form, and disease is often transmitted by drinking contaminated water. As depicted in these SEMs, in the intestine, cysts are stimulated to liberate trophozoites. Cysts can be shed in fecal material, and can, thereafter, remain viable for several months in appropriate environmental conditions. Cysts can also be transferred directly from person-to-person, as a result of poor hygiene.
 

Content Providers(s): CDC/ Dr. Stan Erlandsen 
Creation Date: 1999 
Photo Credit: Dr. Stan Erlandsen 
Links: 
 CDC - Div. of Parasitic Diseases (DPDx); Giardiaisis 

 CDC - Nat. Center for Zoonotic, Vector-borne, and Enteric Disease; Giardiasis: Fact Sheet 
 

COPYRIGHT RESTRICTIONS: None - This image is in the public domain and thus free of any copyright restrictions. As a matter of courtesy we request that the content provider be credited and notified in any public or private usage of this image.

(The following applies to the image of the original bug, which I processed, but didn't use.)

This scanning electron micrograph (SEM) clearly showed the ventral surface of a Giardia muris trophozoite. The ventral adhesive disk resembles a suction cup, where overlapping microtubules in the cytoplasm form a number-6-shaped figure. Giardia muris has four pairs of flagella that are responsible for the organism’s motility. The adhesive disk facilitates adherence of the protozoan to the intestinal surface.
The protozoan Giardia causes the diarrheal disease called giardiasis. Giardia species exist as free-swimming (by means of flagella) trophozoites, and as egg-shaped cysts. It is the cystic stage, which facilitates the survival of these organisms under harsh environmental conditions. The cyst is considered the infective form, and disease is often transmitted by drinking contaminated water. As depicted in these SEMs, in the intestine, cysts are stimulated to liberate trophozoites. Cysts can be shed in fecal material, and can, thereafter, remain viable for several months in appropriate environmental conditions. Cysts can also be transferred directly from person-to-person, as a result of poor hygiene.

Figure 3.15 Bit-plane reconstruction

>> % Use bit planes from Fig. 3.14
>> % Reconstruct with the 2 through 4 higher-order bit planes. 
>> f = imread('Fig0314(a)(trophozoite).tif');
>> B = im2bitplanes(f);
>> g2 = bitplanes2im(B,[8 7]); % The images are of class double
>> g3 = bitplanes2im(B,[8 7 6]);
>> g4 = bitplanes2im(B,[8 7 6 5]); 
>> % Difference between g4 and the original image
>> d = im2double(f) - g4; % Max difference is 0.0588 (0.0588x255 = 15 intensity values on the scale [0, 255]).  Min diff is 0, so all values are positive.
>> % Scale the difference so that it will be more visible.
>> d = intScaling4e(d);
>> figure, imshow(g2)
>> figure, imshow(g3)
>> figure, imshow(g4)
>> figure, imshow(d)
>> imwrite(g2, 'Fig0315(a)(reconstruction_with_bitplanes_8_7).tif','compression','none','resolution',608)
>> imwrite(g3, 'Fig0315(b)(reconstruction_with_bitplanes_8_7_6).tif','compression','none','resolution',608)
>> imwrite(g4, 'Fig0315(c)(reconstruction_with_bitplanes_8_7_6_5).tif','compression','none','resolution',608)
>> imwrite(d, 'Fig0315(d)(difference between original and (c)).tif','compression','none','resolution',608)


NOTES for discussion: The maximum difference difference between the original image and (c) is only 15 intensity levels. If shown without scaling, it would appear black. We show it scaled to the range [0 255] to show the differences.

Fig. 3.25 Histogram equalization of hidden horse image

>> f = imread('Fig0324(a)(hidden horse).tif');
>> % Obtain the histogram equalization intensity transformation function to show in book
>> hfn = imhist(f)/numel(f);
>> thf = cumsum(hfn);
>> % Histogram equalized image.
>> g = histeq(f, 256);
>> % Normalized histogram of equalized image
>> hng = imhist(g)/numel(g);
>> %% Plot the results and format on the MATLAB desktop
>> figure, plot(255*thf) % This will be Fig 3.25(a) (multiply by 255 because max cumsum is 1)
>> figure, bar(hng,0)  % This will be Fig 3.25(c)
>> % Write out image
>> imwrite(g, 'Fig0325(b)(histogram equalized image).tif', 'compression','none', 'resolution',452)

[MAYBE NOT SHOW THE CDF SINCE IT WAS ALREADY EXPLAINED IN FIG 3.20 (EQUALIZATION OF SPACE CRAFT IMAGE)

**************************************************************************
Fig 3.26 Histogram specification of hidden horse image

>> f = imread('Fig0324(a)(hidden horse).tif');
>> % Specified histogram
>> p = manualhist; % This function provides a plot of the specified histogram. Format it manually on the MATLAB desktop.
>> % The following shows the dialog that appears and the inputs that have to be supplied manually
>> % Enter m1, sig1, m2, sig2, A1, A2, k OR x to quit: 0.125,0.05,0.9,0.03,1,.05,0.0018 %This are the manually supplied inputs
>> % Enter m1, sig1, m2, sig2, A1, A2, k OR x to quit:x 
>> % Obtain the histogram-specified image. 
>> g = histeq(f,p); % This is a MATLAB (IPT) function.
>> figure, imshow(g)
>> % Get the transformation function of the specified histogram.
>> tsh = cumsum(p);
>> figure, plot(255*tsh) % The 255 is needed bacause tsh is normalized to 1, and we want a plot of intensities in vs out, in the scale [0, 255].
>> %% To obtain the actual function for mapping, we take the inverse mapping of tsh, as usual. This can be done simply by flipping  
%% tsh vertically.  Do this in Illustrator, and code it with a different line style, like dashes. Note that we are not doing
%% mappings here--Rather, we use histeq(f,p) to do the processing.
>> % Normalized histogram of histogram-specified image.
>> hns = imhist(g)/numel(g);
>> figure, bar(hns, 0)
>> imwrite(g, 'Fig0326(c)(result of histogram specification).tif','compression','none','resolution',452)


NOTES about points to make when explaining figure:
1) The specified histogram is a slight variation of the original histogram, designed lighten the image a little (hence the offset) and move the dark end of the histogram a little bit higher.  The variance of the lower peak is a slight increase over the original to increase the dynamic range in the dark area.

2) The transformation function G^(-1) is simply G (the transformation function of the specified histogram) flipped about the horizontal axis and then rotated counterclockwise 90 degreea. G-1 is applied to the histogram equalized image of the previous example.

3) Horizontal axis is input intensity and vertical axis is output intensity in (a) and (b). In (d) the horizontal is intensity and the vertical is probability.

Figure 3.27 Line drawing.


**************************************************************************
Figure 3.28  Exact specification of uniform histogram of hidden horse

>> f = imread('Fig0324(a)(hidden horse).tif'); %452 dpi image to give 2.3" across
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> % Construct a  non-normalized uniform histogram.
>> z = 1:256;
>> fun = trapezmf(z,0,0, 256,256); % See DIPUM 2E Sec 3.6 for an explanation of this function.
>> H = fun2hist(fun, M*N); % This is a new DIP4E function that I wrote.
>> % "Normal" histogram equalized image.
>> geq = histeq(f, 256);
>> figure, imshow(geq)
>> % Histogram specified image with the uniform histogram
>> gsp = spechist(f, H);
>> figure, imshow(gsp)
>> figure, bar(imhist(gsp), 0)  % Save as eps and process by hand using Illustrator.
>> imwrite(f,'Fig0328(a)(hidden horse).tif','compression','none','resolution',452)
>> imwrite(geq,'Fig0328(b)(hidden horse-hist equalized).tif','compression','none','resolution',452)
>> imwrite(gsp,'Fig0328(c)(hidden horse-hist spec uniform).tif','compression','none','resolution',452)


**************************************************************************
Figure 3.29  Manipulating the uniform histogram.  Uniform/ramp combo

>> f = imread('Fig0324(a)(hidden horse).tif'); %452 dpi image to give 2.3" across. 547 dpi to give 1.9028" across.
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> % Generate a function whose first part is flat (uniform) and its tail end is a ramp.
>> z = 1:256;
>> fun = trapezmf(z,0,0, 64,256); % See DIPUM 2E Sec 3.6 for an explanation of this function. Tried 0, 64, 128, 192-- 0 and 64 gave the best results in terms of reducing noise and the washed out appearance.
>> % Generate an un-normalized histogram with the shape of this function and whose sum is M*N
>> H = fun2hist(fun, M*N); % This is one of my functions.
>> figure, bar(H, 0); % Save as eps and process with illustrator.
>> % Generate an image with this histogram
>> gramp = exacthist(f, H);
>> figure, imshow(gramp)
>> Hg = imhist(gramp, 256);
>> figure, bar(Hg, 0)  % Save as eps and process with Illustrator.
>> imwrite(gramp, 'Fig0329(b)(horse image enhanced with uniform-ramp combo histogram).tif','compression','none','resolution',452)


**************************************************************************
Figure 3.30 A case in which exact histogram specification doesn't work.

>> f = imread('Fig0330(a)(mars phobos moon).tif'); %359 dpi for a width of 1.9028" (3 images across both columns)
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> Hf = imhist(f, 256);
>> figure, imshow(f)
>> figure, plot(Hf)
>> % Specify a uniform histogram
>> H(1:256) = M*N/256; % In this case this does not yield a whole number, so process histogrm with function fun2hist.
>> H = fun2hist(H, M*N);
>> % Exact histogram specification
>> g = exacthist(f, H);
>> Hg = imhist(g);
>> figure, plot(Hg) %Save as eps and process with Illustrator.
>> figure, imshow(g)  % Not a good result because of large black areas.  Mask those out--see next figure

>> imwrite(g,'Fig0330(c)(result of poor exact hist equal).tif','compression','none','resolution',359)

CAPTION NOTE:  Give image size 1000 x 683

**************************************************************************
Figure 3.31 Masking for a better result

>> f = imread('Fig0330(a)(mars phobos moon).tif'); %359 dpi for a width of 1.9028" (3 images across both columns)
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> idx = find(f == 0);
>> mask = ones(size(f));
>> mask(idx) = 0;
>> figure, imshow(mask)
>> % Exact histogram-equalize the masked image
>> H(1:256) = M*N/256; % In this case this does not yield a whole number, so process histogrm with function fun2hist.
>> H = fun2hist(H, M*N);
>> gmasked = exacthist(f, H, mask);
>> figure, imshow(gmasked)  % Better result, but a little dark.
>> % Generate a histogram where the upper intensities go up
>> z = 1:256;
>> sig = 0.065 + sigmamf(z,32,256);   
>> Hup = fun2hist(sig, M*N);
>> figure, bar(Hup, 0) % Same thing, but in bar format instead of a plot. This is figure (c)--top
>> [gup, Hg] = exacthist(f, Hup, mask);
>> figure, imshow(gup)
>> figure, bar(Hg, 0)% Save as eps and process with Illustrator. This is figure (c)--bottom
>> imwrite(mask, 'Fig0331(a)(mask).tif','compression','none','resolution',359)
>> imwrite(gmasked, 'Fig0331(b)(result of exact hist eq the masked image).tif','compression','none','resolution',359)
>> imwrite(gup, 'Fig0331(d)(exact hist specified masked image).tif','compression','none','resolution',359)

NOTE: When discussing figure, mention that the 0th component of the masked specified histogram has been deleted since interest is only on the histo of the masked area.

>> % Filter with 21 x 21 box kernel

>> figure, imshow(gbox21,[])

TO CHANGE LOW AND HIGH SETTINGS OF THE SHADE OF THE RESULTING PLOT
1) Edit/Colormap
2) Double-click below the lowest bar to change the lowest gray--Same for the high bar.
3) A single click below a bar introduces a new color breakpoint that can be slided up and down the gray scale.

To get part (b) (values of 3x3 kernel):
>> w = gaussiankernel(3,'sampled',1,1);
>> constant = sum(w(:));

Figure 3.42 Gaussian filtering of character test pattern.

>> f = im2double(imread('testpattern1024.tif'));
>> % 21x21 Gaussian kernel. Need sig = 3.5 for the 6times rule.
>> gauss3pt5 = gaussiankernel(21,'sampled',3.5,1);
>> % Normalize
gauss3pt5 = gauss3pt5/sum(gauss3pt5(:)) ;
>> % Filter. Deafault padding is zero padding.
ggauss3pt5 = imfilter(f,gauss3pt5);
% As the following image shows, blurring is not comparable to 21x21 box filter.
figure, imshow(ggauss3pt5)

>> % To acieve comparable results, need sig = 7, meaning a gaussian filter of size 43x43
>> gauss7 = gaussiankernel(43,'sampled',7,1);
>> gauss7 = gauss7/sum(gauss7(:));
>> ggauss7 = imfilter(f,gauss7);
>> figure, imshow(ggauss7)

% Save results.
imwrite(ggauss3pt5,'Fig0342(b)(test pattern lowpass gauss 21by21 sig 3pt5).tif','compression','none','resolution',538)
imwrite(ggauss7,'Fig0342(c)(test pattern lowpass gauss 43by43 sig 7).tif','compression','none','resolution',538)



**************************************************************************
Fiure 3.43 Showing that Gaussian filters don't have to be greater than 3 sig. (total size 6 sig x 6 sig)

>> f = im2double(imread('testpattern1024.tif'));

>> gauss43 = gaussiankernel(43,'sampled',7,1); % Approx 6 sig
>> gauss85 = gaussiankernel(85,'sampled',7,1); % Approx 12 sig

% Normalize the filters
>> gauss43 = gauss43/sum(gauss43(:));
>> gauss85 = gauss85/sum(gauss85(:));

% Now filter (default padding is zero padding)
>> ggauss43 = imfilter(f, gauss43);
>> ggauss85 = imfilter(f, gauss85);

% Compare the 85x85 result with the 43x43 result.

>> diff = imsubtract(ggauss43, ggauss85);
>> figure, imshow(diff)
>> 255*max(diff(:))

	0.7469 % Less than one intensity level on an 8-bit scale.

>> imwrite(ggauss43,'Fig0343(a)(test pattern lowpass gauss 43x43 sig 7).tif','compression','none','resolution',538)
>> imwrite(ggauss85,'Fig0343(b)(test pattern lowpass gauss 85x85 sig 7).tif','compression','none','resolution',538)
>> imwrite(diff,'Fig0343(c)(difference between the two).tif','compression','none','resolution',538)

Figure 3.44 Comparing box and Gaussian lowpass filtering.

>> f =uint8(zeros(1024));
>> %f(128:896,192:256)=255;
>> f(128:896,192:320)=255;
>> figure,imshow(f)
>> improfile  % Save as eps and process with illustrator.

>> box=ones(71);
>> box = box/sum(box(:));
>> gbox = imfilter(f,box,'replicate');
>> figure, imshow(gbox)
>> improfile  % Save as eps and process with illustrator.

>> gaussian = gaussiankernel(151, 'sampled',25,1);
>> gaussian = gaussian/sum(gaussian(:));
>> ggauss = imfilter(f, gaussian, 'replicate');
>> figure, imshow(ggauss)
>> improfile % Save as eps and process with illustrator.

>> imwrite(f, 'Fig0344(a)(rectangle).tif', 'compression','none','resolution',538)

**************************************************************************
Figure 3.48  Shading correction using lowpass filtering--uses lp filtering to estimate the shading function, and the image model to correct shading.

>> f = im2double(checkerboard(128)); % 8 squares x 128 = 1024 image.
>> % The white squares on the right half of this image are gray (0.50) by default. Make them 1.0).
>> f = im2double(f > 0.5); % Use im2double because result of operation produces a logical image.
>> % Create an image 4 times larger than f.
>> f1 = zeros(2048);
>> f1(1:1024,1:1024) = f;
>> f1(1025:2048,1025:2048)=f;
>> f1(1:1024,1025:2048)=f;
>> f1(1025:2048,1:1024)=f;
>> f = f1;
>> clear f1
>> % Make white squares light gray so that they'll show diffrent from the page background in the book.
>> idx = find(f == 1);
>> f(idx) = 0.99;
>> [M,N] = size(f);
>> shade = ishade(M, N, 0.001, 1.0,'ramp', -45);
>> g = shade.*f;
>> figure, imshow(g) 
   % Specify a gaussian lowpass filter 4 times the size of each square (128x4 = 512), and a stand deviation of 128 (size of squares).
>> w = fspecial('gaussian', 512, 128);
>> h = imfilter(g, w, 'symmetric'); % This is an estimate of the shading.
>> % Correct the shaded image by dividing it by the estimate of the shading.
>> fout = g./h;
>> % Scale fout for display
>> fout = intScaling4e(fout);
>> figure, imshow(fout)
>> % Scale estimate for display
>> hs = intScaling4e(h);
>> figure, imshow(hs)

   % Write out results--1076 dpi to get images 1.9028" across. Fits 3 images across both columns.
>> imwrite(g, 'Fig03XZ(a)(shaded checkerboard image).tif','compression','none','resolution',1076)
>> imwrite(hs, 'Fig03XZ(b)(estimate of shading pattern).tif','compression','none','resolution',1076)
>> imwrite(fout, 'Fig03XZ(c)((a) divided by (b)).tif','compression','none','resolution',1076)

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0353(a)(blurry moon).tif'));

>> %Scale lap4 so that it'll range from 0 to 255.

Figure 3.56 Line drawing--Unsharp Masking Profiles

Approach:  Generate a ramp image and do the processing on it. For the profiles
just take a horizontal cross section through the middle of it.

% Generate image.
>> g=synim(1024,1024,1,256,384,254);  %Function synim is my function{{{NOTE TO ME: SEE FUNCTION ISHADE}}}
>> pg = g(512,1:end); % Profile
>> plot(pg)	% Adjust x axis to 200:820 and y axis to -50:320
>> h1=fspecial('average',100);
>> ga=imfilter(g,h1,'replicate'); %Smooth image.
>> pa=ga(512,1:end); %Profile of smoothed image
>> figure,plot(pa);	% Adjust x axis to 200:820 and y axis to -50:320
>> pu = pg - pa; % Unsharp profie
>> figure, plot(pu) % Adjust x axis to 200:820 and y axis to -50:50 (original -15 to 15 was too high) >> ps=pg + 2*pu; % Profile of sharp image.  Used a 2 to scale so that it would look reasonable
			   % with the scaled pu. Otherwise sharp hump is too small.
>> figure, plot(ps) % Adjust x axis to 200:820 and y axis to -50:320
       			   
% axis off and edited the windows. Then Saved the results in eps format.

Figure 3.60 Line drawing.


**************************************************************************
Figures 3.61 Zone plate image. 
		3.62 1-D Lowpass filter and 2-D generated from it.
		3.63 Lowpass of zone plate image.
		3.64 Lowpass, highpass, bandreject and bandpass from lowpass

% Generate an image that will print at 2 x 2 inches. Zoneplates have aliasing issues, and InDesign converts all gray-scale
% images to 300 DPI. The image I generated is 597x597 which will be near 2" x 2" when printed at 300 dpi. It is void of aliasing 
% and is sufficient to illustrate lowpass, highpass, bandreject, and bandpass filtering. I blurred it slightly for additional insurance
% against aliasing.
>> f = zoneplate(8.2,.0275,0);
>> w = [1 2 1;2 4 2;1 2 1]/16; % Gaussian filter.
>> f = imfilter(f, w, 'replicate');
>> % Save for posting.  SAVE also  as Fig0361.mat to post in Web site.  That way, floating point values are preserved. The commnands are save('Fig0361.mat', 'f').  To get it back, type:  load Fig0361  (no single quotes needed). Actually, it's OK to save image as tif file. Just make sure to use im2double when reading it in.

>> imwrite(f,'Fig0361(zoneplate image 597x597 300 dpi).tif','compression','none','resolution',300)

>> % Read image in.
>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0361(zoneplate image 597x597 300 dpi).tif')); % Needs to be double when read in, to illustrate filtering effects.

>> % Lowpass filtering.
>> % 1-D lowpass filter (Use MATLAB's Signal Processing Toolbox)
>> lp = fir1(128, 0.1); 

>> % 2-D Separable lowpass filter
>> lp2s = lp'*lp;

>> % 2-D Circularly symmetric lowpass filter.
>> lp2c = ftrans2(lp);

>>  % Graphics for Figs. 3.62(a) and (b).  Save as eps and process with Illustrator.
>>  figure, plot(lp)  
>>  figure, mesh(lp2c(1:2:end,1:2:end));
>>  colormap([0 0 0]);
>>  axis off

>> % Filter image  with both of these filters to show that separable filter gives a 
>> % "squarish" result.
>> glps = imfilter(f, lp2s, 'symmetric');
>> glpc = imfilter(f, lp2c, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(glps)
>> figure, imshow(glpc)

>> % Highpass from lowpass.
>> ghp = imsubtract(f, glpc); % OR, 
>> % Can also do like this:
>> % Highpass from lowpass: Subtract lowpass filter from (centered) impulse.
>> % Construct 1-D impulse.
>> M = numel(lp);
>> center = ceil(M/2);
>> del(1:M) = 0;
>> del(center) = 1;
>> hp = del - lp;
>> % Get circularly symmetric filter from 1-D filter.
>> hp2c = ftrans2(hp);
>> ghpc = imfilter(f, hp2c, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(ghpc)

>> % Bandreject from lowpass (and highpass)
>> % Lower the lowpass filter and increase the highpass filter cutoffs.
>> lp1 = fir1(128, 0.06);
>> lp2 = fir1(128, 0.12);
>> hp2 = del - lp2;
>> % Bendreject filter
>> hbr = lp1 + hp2;
>> % Circularly symmetric
>> hbrc = ftrans2(hbr);
>> gbr = imfilter(f, hbrc, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(gbr)

>> % Bandpass from bandreject
>> hbp = del - hbr;
>> hbpc = ftrans2(hbp);
>> gbp = imfilter(f, hbpc, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(gbp);

>> % The highpass and bandpass results have negative values that are clipped at black. Show scaled images.
>> ghpcs = intScaling4e(ghpc);
>> figure, imshow(ghpcs)
>> gbps = intScaling4e(gbp);
>> figure, imshow(gbps)

>> % Write results

>> imwrite(glps, 'Fig0363(a)(lowpass with separable filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300)
>> imwrite(glpc, 'Fig0363(b)(lowpass with circularly symmtric filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300)

>> imwrite(glpc, 'Fig0364(a)(lowpass with circularly symmetric filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300)
>> imwrite(ghpc, 'Fig0364(b)(highpass with circularly symmetric filter-unscaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300) 
>> imwrite(ghpcs, 'Fig0364(c)(highpass with circularly symmetric filter-scaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300)
>> imwrite(gbr, 'Fig0364(d)(bandreject with circularly symmetric filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300)
>> imwrite(gbp, 'Fig0364(e)(bandpass with circularly symmetric filter-unscaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300) 
>> imwrite(gbps, 'Fig0364(f)(bandpass with circularly symmetric filter-scaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 300)

**************************************************************************
Figure 3.65 Enhancement of skeleton bone scan image

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0365(a)(skeleton original).tif'));
>> figure, imshow(f)
>> % Laplacian
>> w = [-1 -1 -1;-1 8 -1;-1 -1 -1];
>> gL = imfilter(f, w, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(gL)
>> % Image needs scaling (for display only)
>> gLs = intScaling4e(gL);
>> figure, imshow(gLs)

>> % Sharpen the image by adding gL to f:
>> gSharp = f + gL;
>> figure, imshow(gSharp)

>> % gSharp is a very noisy image. Combine the Laplacian with the smoothed gradient
>> % to get "the best of both worlds" (see book for detailed explanation).
>> % Compute the magnitude of the gradient using absolute values.
>> gx = [-1 -2 -1;0 0 0;1 2 1];
>> gy = [-1 0 1;-2 0 2;-1 0 1];
>> G = abs(imfilter(f, gx, 'symmetric')) + abs(imfilter(f, gy, 'symmetric'));
>> figure, imshow(G)

>> % Smooth the gradient image.
>> waverage = ones(5);
>> waverage = waverage/sum(waverage(:));
>> Gaverage = imfilter(G, waverage, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(Gaverage)

>> % Multiply the Laplacian-enhanced image (gSharp) and Smoothed gardient:
>> LG = gSharp.*Gaverage;
>> figure,  imshow(LG)

>> % Add the LG to f to obtain an edge-enhanced image
>> gEE = f + LG;
>> figure, imshow(gEE)

>> % Image gEE is very sharp, as desired, but the overall dynamic range is still
>> % somewhat low. Perform a power-law (gamma) transformation to remedy this. After
>> % some trials, gamma = 0.5 and c = 1 yielded good results.
>> gfinal = intrans(gEE,'gamma',0.5); 
>> figure, imshow(gfinal)

>> imwrite(gLs, 'Fig0365(b)(scaled Laplacian).tif','compression','none', 'resolution',300)
>> imwrite(gSharp, 'Fig0365(c)(image + Laplacian).tif','compression','none', 'resolution',300)
>> imwrite(G, 'Fig0365(d)(Sobel gradient).tif','compression','none', 'resolution',300)

Figure 3.73 Obtaining the percent maturity for the fruit example used 
throughout Section 3.9 Fuzzy Techniques for Image Processing.

>> % Compute input (color) membership functions. Range of independent variable: [0, 1].
>> ugreen = fuzzymf('triang',200,0,1,[0.2,.2,.2]);
>> uyellow = fuzzymf('triang',200,0,1,[.5,.25,.25]);
>> ured = fuzzymf('triang',200,0,1,[0.78,.22,.22]);
>> figure, plot(ugreen)
>> hold on
>> plot(uyellow)
>> hold on
>> plot(ured)

>> % Compute maturity (output) membership functions. Range of independent variable: [0, 100].
>> uverd = fuzzymf('trapez',101,0,100,[0,10,0,20]);
>> uhalf = fuzzymf('trapez',101,0,100,[38,52,19,18]);
>> umat = fuzzymf('trapez',101,0,100,[80,100,25,0]);
>> figure, plot(uverd)
>> hold on
>> plot(uhalf)
>> hold on
>> plot(umat)

>> % Combine membership functions into single arrays.
>> inmf = [ugreen; uyellow; ured];
>> outmf = [uverd; uhalf; umat];

>> % Rules matrix (see function fuzzeval)
>> R = [1;2;3];
>> % Fuzzify and evaluate rules.
>> z = .705
>> rule_strength = fuzzyeval(R, inmf, z, 1);
>> % Perform implication.
>> q = fuzzyimp(rule_strength,outmf);
>> % Aggregate and defuzzify.
>> defuzz = fuzzyad(q);

>> % If need to blurr original image to reduce aliasing can use Phoshop--A Gaussian blur with a radius of 4 seems mild and effective.
>> % But wait for a test print from PH before blurring the images.
>> % Works fine if f is saved as tif and then read in. Make sure to use f = im2double('Fig0361(a)(zoneplate image 3001x3001).tif');

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0361(zoneplate image 3001x3001).tif'));

>> % 1-D lowpass filter (Use MATLAB's Signal Processing Toolbox)
>> lp = fir1(128, 0.06); % The resulting filter has 129 elements.

>> % 2-D Separable lowpass filter
>> lp2s = lp'*lp;

>> % 2-D Circularly symmetric lowpass filter.
>> lp2c = ftrans2(lp);

>> % Graphics for Figs. 3.62(a) and (b).  Save as eps and process with Illustrator.
>> % figure, plot(lp)  
>> % figure, mesh(lp2c(1:2:end,1:2:end));
>> % colormap([0 0 0]);
>> % axis off

>> % Filter image  with both of these filters to show that separable filter gives a 
>> % "squarish" result.
>> glps = imfilter(f, lp2s, 'symmetric');
>> glpc = imfilter(f, lp2c, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(glps)
>> figure, imshow(glpc)

>> % Highpass from lowpass.
>> ghp = imsubtract(f, glpc); % OR, 
>> % Can also do like this:
>> % Construct 1-D impulse.
>> M = numel(lp);
>> center = ceil(M/2);
>> del(1:M) = 0;
>> del(center) = 1;
>> hp = del - lp;
>> % Get circularly symmetric filter from 1-D filter.
>> hp2c = ftrans2(hp);
>> ghpc = imfilter(f, hp2c, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(ghpc)

>> % Bandreject from lowpass (and highpass)
>> % Lower the lowpass filter and increase the highpass filter cutoffs.
>> lp1 = fir1(128, 0.03);
>> lp2 = fir1(128, 0.08);
>> hp2 = del - lp2;
>> % Bendreject filter
>> hbr = lp1 + hp2;
>> % Circularly symmetric
>> hbrc = ftrans2(hbr);
>> gbr = imfilter(f, hbrc, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(gbr)
 
>> % Bandpass from bandreject
>> hbp = del - hbr;
>> hbpc = ftrans2(hbp);
>> gbp = imfilter(f, hbpc, 'symmetric');
>> figure, imshow(gbp);

>> % The highpass and bandpass results have negative values that are clipped at black. Show scaled images.
>> ghpcs = intScaling4e(ghpc);
>> figure, imshow(ghpcs)
>> gbps = intScaling4e(gbp);
>> figure, imshow(gbps)

>> % Note: the following images are written in 1500 dpi to produce 2x2 size. 

>> imwrite(glps, 'Fig0363(a)(lowpass with separable filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500)
>> imwrite(glpc, 'Fig0363(b)(lowpass with circularly symmtric filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500)

>> imwrite(glpc, 'Fig0364(a)(lowpass with circularly symmetric filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500)
>> imwrite(ghpc, 'Fig0364(b)(highpass with circularly symmetric filter-unscaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500) 
>> imwrite(gbr, 'Fig0364(d)(bandreject with circularly symmetric filter).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500)
>> imwrite(gbp, 'Fig0364(e)(bandpass with circularly symmetric filter-unscaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500) 
>> imwrite(ghpcs, 'Fig0364(c)(highpass with circularly symmetric filter-scaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500)
>> imwrite(gbps, 'Fig0364(f)(bandpass with circularly symmetric filter-scaled).tif', 'compression','none','resolution', 1500)

(Cut off frequency of highpass filter should be lower than for the lowpass filter, so their cascade passes a band. But remember, the FT of a Gaussian is a Gaussian with the inverse of the value of the variance. This means that we specify a higher variance for the HP filter in the spatial domain to get a lower variance in the frequency domain.)

Figure 4.4 Fourier transform of pulse (sinc function).

Generated with the following function:

function s = mysinc(L, H, k, inc)
% Computes the 1D sinc function: sinc(kx)=sin(pi*kx)/(pi*kx). L and H are
% the limits for the computation, and inc is the sampling increment to 
% to use.  For example if L =-5, H = 5 and inc=0.01, the sampling interval
% generated is x = -5:.01:5.
x = L:inc:H;
s = sin(pi*k*x)./(pi*k*x + eps);
% sin(0) = 1
J = find(x==0);
s(J)=1;

Generate sinc function for book figure:

>> s = mysinc(-9.5,9.5,1.0,0.0001);

Then: for Fig. 4.4(b):

>> plot(s)
>> axis off

Then, in the figure window, change background to white, the lines to black, and the line 
thickness to 1.0.  Saved as eps file. Later, when the figure was rescaled in Corel, the line
width had to be reset to 1.0.

For Fig. 4.4(c)

>> plot(abs(s))
>> axis off

Did as in 4.4(b) but in addition set the vertical scale to correspond to the same scale as
in (b) so that the figures would be proportionally accurate. 

In both figures chopped off a little from the end (in Corel) so that they would fit
better.  These figures could be regenrated using the sinc function aboove by shortening
the limits, but I just exported them as eps files from Corel once I had chopped up and 
rescaled them to generate the composite .cdr figure.

Figure 4.14 A 2-D box function and its spectrum (2-D sinc).

Spectrum computed and plotted as follows:

function [f, Spec] = example4pt5(A,S,T,M,N)
% Generate function.
f = zeros(M,N);
f(1:S,1:T)=A;
% Compute Fourier transform.
F = fft2(f);
% Center the transform.
F = fftshift(F);
Spec= abs(F) + eps;

>> [f, Spec] = example4pt5(1,6,8,1024,1024);
>> mesh(Spec(10:20:end,10:20:end))
>> axis off
>> colormap([0 0 0])

Changed the line width to 0.5

Then saved it as an .eps file.

Figure 4.17 Vector drawing of sampling grid and bands showing aliasing effects. 


**************************************************************************
Figure 4.18 Sampled chekerboard image to illustrate aliasing.

Wrote a program to generate sampled squares. The input to the program are
delX and M.  M is the square image size in pixels. delX*M is the number of 
squares across a row of the image. The width of each sqaures is 1/delX pixels.
The program is interpreted as squares having unit width and we sample across
at a given sampling rate. The pattern of squares generated in the image 
thus depends on the specified value of delX.

The objective of the program was to generate images to illustrate aliasing.
The period of the squares is 2*(1/delX).  Need more than two samples per period
to avoid aliasing, so delX has to be delX < 1 to avoid aliasing.

Generated the following images with M = 96:
                                     
delX  | No.Samples/square | No. Squares generated/line (1/delX)
0.0625          16.0                 6.0      
0.1667           6.0                16.0
1.05             0.95238           100.8   (aliasing)         
2.084            0.47985           208.4   (severe aliasing--But 8 perfect squares appear per line)

Function calls to generate images:

>> g=checkerimage(0.0625,96); imshow(g)
>> imwrite(g,'Fig4.18(a)(delX.eq.0.0625).tif','compression','none')
>> g=checkerimage(0.1667,96); imshow(g)
>> imwrite(g,'Fig4.18(b)(delX.eq.0.1167).tif','compression','none')
>> g=checkerimage(1.05,96); imshow(g)
>> imwrite(g,'Fig4.18(c)(delX.eq.1.05).tif','compression','none')
>> g=checkerimage(2.084,96);imshow(g)
>> imwrite(g,'Fig4.18(d)(delX.eq.2.084).tif','compression','none')

I then scaled the images to 2.25" at 427 dpi, and used only the top half.

Here's the program (its in my DIP4E functions):

function g = checkerimage(delX,M)
% Generates a checkerboard image in which the squares are 1/delX pixels wide.
% and there are delX*M squares in the checkerboard. The ouput image is 
% generated by sampling the checkerbaord every delX pixels to generate an 
% M x M image. delX does not have to be an integer. For example,
% delX = 0.0125 with M = 400 generates an checkerboard image of size 
% 400 x 400 pixels, with 5 squares per row (there are 5 rows of squarea)
% each square being 80 pixels on the side.
%
% The program is based on the assumption that wer are sampling squares of
% size 1 on the side, with the first square being black (0). Thus, if we
% look at one line, if the coordinate is in the interval [1,2), then the
% function is black (0) .  If in the interval [2,3) then the function is
% white (1) and so on.  In other words, if the integer part of the interval
% is odd, we have a black square (i.e., values 1, 1.2, 1.999999 all should
% yield values of 1). If the integer part of the inverval is even we have a
% white (1) square. 
%
% Picking delX less than 1 gives more than one sample per interval. Picking
% delX greater than 1 gives less than one sample per interval, causing
% aliasing.
% 
% CAUTION:  Because the number of samples is fixed at M, it is possible
% dependng on delX to get fractional squares with delX < 1. Be careful
% not to confuse this with aliasing.
%
% This program was written to illustrate alising, in which there are
% multiple squares between samples. For ex. if delX = 11.5 and M = 400,
% we will be sampling at a rate that is just 1 sample every more than 10
% intervals. This will cause aliasing.

% Generate sampling intervals.
kx = 1 - delX;
for I = 1:M
   kx = kx + delX +eps ;
   val = 1; % intially set to white.
   % Extract integer part. If odd,set sample value to black. Else to white.
      if isodd(floor(kx))
         val = 0;
      end
    r(I)=val;   
end

% A sampled column is equal to a sampled row
c = r;

% Generate the image. For any pixel, if both value of r and c are 0, set the
% pixel to 0. Otherwise set to 1.
g(1:M,1:M) = 1; % all white initially.
for I = 1:M
   for J = 1:M
      if (r(I)== 0 & c(J) == 0)
         g(I, J) = 0;
      elseif (r(I) == 1 & c(J) == 0)
         g(I, J) = 1;
      elseif (r(I) == 0 & c(J) == 1)
         g(I, J) = 1;
      elseif (r(I) == 1 & c(J) == 1)
         g(I, J) = 0;
      end
   end
end


The following function is included in the DIPUM2E functions.
function D = isodd(A)
%ISODD Determines which elements of an array are odd numbers.
%   E = ISODD(A) returns a logical array, D, of the same size as A,
%   with 1s (TRUE) in the locations corresponding to odd numbers
%   (i.e., . . . -3, -1, 1, 3, . . . )in A, and 0s (FALSE) elsewhere. 
%   A must be a numeric array.

%   Copyright 2004 R. C. Gonzalez, R. E. Woods, & S. L. Eddins
%   Projects and Solutions for Digital Image Processing Using MATLAB.
%   $Revision: 1.3 $  $Date: 2004/03/15 00:28:22 $

% Check the validity of A.
if ~isnumeric(A)
    error('A must be a numeric array.');
end

A = double(A);
D = floor((A + 1)/2) == ((A + 1)/2);

Figures 4.24 AND 4.25 Spectra and Phase Angles of translated and rotated rectangle.

% Displaced rectangle
>> g=zeros(512);
>> g(108:204, 348:364)=1;
>> G=fft2(g);
>> SG=abs(G);
>> SG=fftshift(SG); %Center the spectrum
>> SG=log10(1 + abs(SG)); % Log transformation
>> SG=SG-min(SG(:)); %Normalize to [0 1] for display. % Could also use function intScaling4e for this, like I did in Fig. 4.23
>> SG=SG/max(SG(:));

>> r = imrotate(f,-45,'bilinear','crop');
>> R=fft2(r);
>> SR=abs(R);
>> SR=fftshift(SR); %Center the spectrum
>> SR=log10(1 + abs(SR)); % Log transformation
>> SR=SR-min(SR(:)); %Normalize to [0 1] for display.
>> SR=SR/max(SR(:));

>> % Compute phase angle of the f, g and r.  They look best if not scaled.
>> fphi = angle(F);
>> gphi = angle(G);
>> rphi = angle(R);

% Make sure it all worked OK
Cf=complex(0,fphi);
Cg=complex(0,gphi);
Freconst=abs(F).*exp(Cf);
frec=real(ifft2(Freconst));
figure, imshow(frec)                %OK
Greconst=abs(G).*exp(Cg);
grec=real(ifft2(Greconst));
figure, imshow(grec)                %OK

imwrite(g, 'Fig0424(a)(translated rectangle).tif','compression','none')
imwrite(SG,'Fig0424(b)(spectrum of translated rectangle).tif','compression','none')
imwrite(r, 'Fig0424(c)(rotated rectangle).tif','compression','none')

**************************************************************************
Figure 4.29 Blown IC with DC term removed.

% NO PADDING--WORKS
>> f=imread('Fig4.28(a)(blown_ic).tif');
>> f=im2double(f);
>> [M,N]=size(f);
>> H=lpfilter('ideal',M,N,0.5);
>> H=imcomplement(H);
>> g=dftfilt(f,H);
>> figure, imshow(g)

% WITH PADDING--Doesn't work.  The reason is:  When pad, the image size is extended, so the
% average value obtained by deleting the DC term is with respect to that extended image. When
% the image is cropped back to original size, the average goes up, so the image will appear
% brighter.

>> f=imread('Fig4.28(a)(blown_ic).tif');
>> f=im2double(f);
>> PQ=paddedsize(size(f));
>> H = lpfilter('ideal',PQ(1),PQ(2),0.5);
>> H=imcomplement(H);
>> g=dftfilt(f,H);
>> figure, imshow(g)

% without padding. gmax=0.5585, gmin = -.4415.  mean(g(:))=5.4306e-015
% with padding: gmax=.8896 gmin=-0.1104  mean(g(:))=0.3311 (should be near zero as above)

**************************************************************************
Figure 4.38 EXAMPLE 4.15 (frequency domain filter from Sobel kernel)

% Do frequency domain first.

>> f = imread('Fig0438(image_of_bld_600_by_600).tif');  
>> f = im2double(f);
>> f = minus1(f); % Multiply by (-1)^x+y
>> h = -fspecial('sobel')'; % This is the kernel shown in Fig. 4.38(a).
>> ht2 = zeros(602,602); %% padding size based on Eqs.(4-98) nand (4-99) DIP4E. See text of Example 4/15
>> ht2(301:303,301:303) = h(1:3,1:3); 	% Place h in center of ht2 to preserve odd symmetry. This is important.
										% The center is at (301,301) but MATLAB starts counting at 1
										% so we have to put the center at (302,302). 					
>> ht2 = minus1(ht2);  % Need (-1)^x+y to make sure H(u,v) is centered.
>> Ht2 = fft2(ht2);  
>> H = imag(Ht2);
>> H = complex(0, H); % Will be multiplying by F, which is complex.
>> H = minus1(H); % To reverse the implied (-1)^x+y in centering h on ht2.
>> PQ = paddedsize(size(f),size(h)); % This function is from DIPUM2E
>> F = fft2(f,PQ(1),PQ(2));
>> G = H.*F;  
>> ge = real(ifft2(G));
>> ge = minus1(ge); % To undo the earlier (-1)^x+y
>> gf = ge(1:600,1:600);
>> gfs = intScaling4e(gf); % gf has negative values. need to scale.
>> figure,imshow(gfs)

>> % Image of Sobel kernel in the frequency domain.
>> Sf = intScaling4e(imag(H));
>> figure, imshow(Sf)

>> % Mesh plot of Sobel kernel in the frequency domain.
>> figure, mesh((imag(H(1:15:end,1:15:end))))
>> colormap([0 0 0])
>> axis off    %Then set background to white in window and save as eps directly from window

% Now do spatial filtering with the Sobel kernel. To get same results as in freq domain must use the 'conv' option.

>> f=imread('Fig0438(image_of_bld_600_by_600).tif');
>> f = im2double(f);
>> gs = imfilter(f, h,'conv');
>> gss = intScaling4e(gs); % gs has negative values. need to scale.
>> figure, imshow(gss)

>> % compare floating point images.
>> d=abs(gs-gf);
>> max(d(:))  % 3.9482e-15
>> min(d(:))  % 0
	
>> % Write results to disk.
>> imwrite(Sf,'Fig0438(b)(freq_domain_sobel_as_image).tif','compression', 'none','resolution',300)
>> imwrite(gfs,'Fig0438(c)(filtered_using_freq_dom_sobel).tif','compression','none','resolution',300);
>> imwrite(gss,'Fig0438(d)(filtered_spatial_dom_sobel).tif','compression','none','resolution',300);					

**************************************************************************

**************************************************************************
Figure 4.40 Image of test pattern and energy enclosed by radii.

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0440(a)(character test pattern-688).tif'));
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> P = 2*M;
>> Q = 2*N;
>> F = fft2(f,P,Q);
>> Power = (abs(F)).^2; % Power spectrum.
>> PT = sum(Power(:)); % Total power.
>> % Compute energy enclosed by various radii.
>> r = [10 30 60 160 460];
>> c = 0;
>> for k = r
>> 	c = c + 1;
>> 	H = lpfilter('ideal', P, Q, k);
>> 	prod = H.*Power;
>> 	E(c) = sum(prod(:))/PT;
>> end
 
>> % Values of E: 0.8688    0.9278    0.9512    0.9757    0.9936 ~~ 86.9%, 92.8%, 95.1%, 97.6%, and 99.4%

>> % To get power removed, subtract these numbers from 100.0: 13.1%, 7.2%, 4.9%, 2.4%, 0.6%

>> % Superimpose circles on spectrum.
>> S = fftshift(log(1 + abs(F)));
>> S = intScaling4e(S);
>> C = zeros(P,Q);
>> for k = 1:5
>> 	C = C | circle(P,Q,r(k),2);
>> end
>> S = intScaling4e(S); % Scale to full range and convert to 8-bits.
>> I = find(C == 1);
>> S(I) = 255;
>> % Reduce size 50% to be the same size as image of test pattern.
>> S = S(1:2:end, 1:2:end);

imwrite(S, 'Fig0440(b)(spectrum with circles superimposed).tif','compression','none','resolution',300)

>> % Generate transfer function.

Figure 4.52 Spatial representation of IHPF, GHPF, and BHPF.
%
% A highpass filter in the frequency domain is 1 - HLP (remember, in MATLAB (1 - A), is the same as (ones(M, N) - A) 
% with A an MxN matrix.
% The inverse DFT of (1 - LP) is a unit impulse in the center of the spatial domain minus the inverse DFT of the lowpass filter.
% The value of the impulse is 1, but the max value of the inverse of the lowpass filter is usually much smaller. So,
% forming the HP filter as (1 - LP) and then taking the inverse produces an image that, when displayed, just shows a bright
% dot in the center. It's best to get the ifft of 1 and the ifft of LP separately and subtract the latter from the former in the % % spatial domain. That way, we can scale one or the other to make their max values closer today in order to see the details of both 
% in an image display.


>> % See Fig. 4.42 for explanation of why double is needed.
>> Hilp = double(lpfilter('ideal',1000,1000, 15)); % Same parameters as in Fig. 4.42 
>> [M, N] = size(Hilp);						 
>> hILP = fftshift(ifft2(Hilp)); % Spatial representation of Hlp 

>> % Constant in the freq. domain. Its inverse will be an impulse.
>> G = ones(M,N);
>> imp = fftshift(ifft2(G)); % imp(M/2 +1, N/2 + 1) is 1 zeros elsewhere. Remember, MATLAB starts counting at 1.

>> % Now subtract one from the other, multiplying one of them by a constant so they'll both shown in image display.
>> hIHP = imp - hILP/max(hILP(:));
>> hIHPs = intScaling4e(hIHP); % Scale for display.
>> figure, imshow(hIHPs)

>> % For Gaussian
>> Hglp = double(lpfilter('gaussian',1000,1000, 15)); % Same parameters as in Fig. 4.42 
>> [M, N] = size(Hglp);						 
>> hGLP = fftshift(ifft2(Hglp)); % Spatial representation of Hlp 

>> % Constant in the freq. domain. Its inverse will be an impulse.
>> G = ones(M,N);
>> imp = fftshift(ifft2(G)); % imp(M/2 +1, N/2 + 1) is 1 zeros elsewhere. Remember, MATLAB starts counting at 1.

>> % Now subtract one from the other, multiplying one of them by a constant so they'll both shown in image display.
>> hGHP = imp - hGLP/max(hGLP(:));
>> hGHPs = intScaling4e(hGHP); % Scale for display.
>> figure, imshow(hGHPs)


>> % For Butterworth
>> Hblp = double(lpfilter('btw',1000,1000, 15, 2)); % Same parameters as in Fig. 4.42 
>> [M, N] = size(Hblp);						 
>> hBLP = fftshift(ifft2(Hblp)); % Spatial representation of Hlp 

>> % Constant in the freq. domain. Its inverse will be an impulse.
>> G = ones(M,N);
>> imp = fftshift(ifft2(G)); % imp(M/2 +1, N/2 + 1) is 1 zeros elsewhere. Remember, MATLAB starts counting at 1.

>> % Now subtract one from the other, multiplying one of them by a constant so they'll both shown in image display.
>> hBHP = imp - hBLP/max(hBLP(:));
>> hBHPs = intScaling4e(hBHP); % Scale for display.
>> figure, imshow(hBHPs)

% Profiles
>> profileI = hIHP(M/2 + 1, 1:end);
>> profileG = hGHP(M/2 + 1, 1:end);
>> profileB = hBHP(M/2 + 1, 1:end);
>> figure, plot(profileI) % Goes below Fig0452(a)% Saved as eps directly from MATLAB
>> axis off
>> figure, plot(profileG) % Goes below Fig0452(b)
>> axis off
>> figure, plot(profileB) % Goes below Fig0452(c)
>> axis off

>> imwrite(hIHPs,'Fig0452(a)(spatial representation of IHPF).tif','compression','none','resolution', 500)
>> imwrite(hGHPs,'Fig0452(b)(spatial representation of GHPF).tif','compression','none','resolution',500)
>> imwrite(hBHPs,'Fig0452(c)(spatial representation of BHPF).tif','compression','none','resolution',500)


NOTE: THe Fourier transform of a circle is a Bessel function, so (a) is not a perfect set of concentric circles.

**************************************************************************
Fig 4.56 Sharpening of blurry moon using the Laplacian in the frequency domain.

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0456(a)(blurry moon).tif'));
>> [M, N] = size(f);
>> P = 2*M;
>> Q = 2*N;
>> [U V] =dftuv(P, Q);
>> % DFTUV puts out single and imwrite wants double. 
>> H = double(-4*(pi)^2*(U.^2 + V.^2)); %This is with respect to the origin, so H is note centered.
>> % Center H.
>> H = fftshift(H);
>> glap = dftfiltering(f, H); % This is the Laplacian image.
>> % Due to filter values and FFT scaling, the range of values of g1 typically is 
>> % far larger than the range of values in the original image.  One way to bring 
>> % the values within a comparable range is to use divide g1 by its maximum value 
>> % so that its maximum value will be 1 (it is important that its negative values be kept).
>> glaps = glap/max(glap(:));
>> g = f - glaps;
>> figure, imshow(g)
>> imwrite(g, 'Fig0459(b)(moon sharpened Laplacian).tif','compression','none','resolution',300)

**************************************************************************
Figure 4.57 Using high-frequency-emphasis to sharpen a Chest X-ray image

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0457(a)(chest xray).tif'));
>> [M, N] = size(f);
>> P = 2*M;
>> Q = 2*N;

>> ghp = dftfiltering(f, H);
>> ghps = intScaling4e(ghp);
>> Hemp = .5+.75*H;
>> gemp=dftfiltering(f, Hemp);
>> gemps = intScaling4e(gemp);
>> geq=histeq(gemp, 256);

>> figure, imshow(f)
>> figure, imshow(ghps)
>> figure, imshow(gemps)
>> figure, imshow(geq)

>> imwrite(ghps,'Fig0457(b)(highpass of (a) gauss 70).tif','compression','none', 'resolution', 300)
>> imwrite(gemps,'Fig0457(c)(high freq emph of (a)).tif','compression','none', 'resolution', 300)

Figure 4.61 Radial crossections of Gaussian bandreject filter transfer functions.

Used the following code with M = 800, W = 120, and C0 = 200

function [H, HL2, Hhigh, HhighS, Hbook] = rcgtemp5(M, W, C0)

%Gaussian radial cross sections

D = 0:M-1;

% lowpass 1:
HL1 = exp(-(D.^2/(W^2)));

%lowpass 2
HL2 = exp(-(D.^2/(4*W^2)));

% highpass fron lowpass
Hhigh = 1 - HL2;

% Bandreject formed by sum of lowpass and highpass Gaussian filters.
H = HL1 + Hhigh; % Plot and save as eps for Fig0461(b)

% highpass with shifted 0-point to C0.
HhighS = (1 - exp(-(D - C0).^2/W^2)); % Plot and save as Fig0461(c)

% Formula in book:
Hbook = 1 - exp(-((D.^2 - C0^2)./(D*W)).^2); % Plot and save as Fig0461(d)

**************************************************************************

Figure 4.64 (Notch filtering of corvette image)

This is a revision from the 3rd edition, in which the function used to generate the filter was not working properly.

f = im2double(imread('Fig0464(a)(car_75DPI_Moire).tif'));
>> figure, imshow(f)
>> [M, N] = size(f);
>> F = fft2(f);
>> S = intScaling4e(log10(1  + abs(fftshift(F)))); % Spectrum
>> figure, imshow(S)
>> % Obtain notch locations manually using function impixelinfo
>> C = [44 54; 85 56; 40 112; 82 112];
>> H = cnotch('btw','reject', M, N, C, 9, 4); % H is uncentered.
>> % Compute spectrum of the filtered transform to show as an image.
>> P = intScaling4e(fftshift(H).*(im2double(S)));
>> figure, imshow(P)
>> % Filter image.
>> % Could also use my function dftfiltering (see how I did Cassini image in the next figure). dftfilt is a DIPUM2E function.
>> g = real(dftfilt(f,H)); % I have a note in DIPUM2E, pg180, to correct dftfilt so that g has no imaginary components. In this example it does, so I'm using real to take care of it.
>> figure, imshow(g)
>> % dftfilt produces a class single result. Convert it to double so that can write to tif file
>> g = im2double(g); 
>> imwrite(S,'Fig0464(b)(spectrum_of_(a)).tif','compression','none','resolution',75)
>> imwrite(P,'Fig0464(c)(notch_butterworth_filter_times_spectrum).tif','compression','none','resolution',75)
>> imwrite(g, 'Fig0464(d)(filtered_image).tif','compression','none','resolution',75)


NOTES ABOUT RESULTS: 

1) Note that D0 is 9, not 3 as indicated in DIP3E.

2) The 75 dpi is OK to use in production because that is the native resolution of the newspaper image being used. It's supposed to be low resolution.

Figure 4.66 Extracting the noise pattern of the Cassini image.

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0465(a)(Casssini image with sinusoidal interference).tif'));
>> [M,N] = size(f);
>> F = fft2(f);
>> Hpass = double(recnotch('pass', 'vertical',M, N, 5, 15, 15)); % recnotch is a DIPUM2E function.
>> % Hpass is an uncentered function, as is F.
>> P = Hpass.*F;
>> SP = intScaling4e(log10(1+abs(fftshift(P)))); 
>> figure, imshow(SP)
>> pattern=intScaling4e(real(fftshift((ifft2(P)))));
>> figure, imshow(pattern)
>> imwrite(SP, 'Fig0466(a)(spetrum of interference pattern).tif','compression','none','resolution',300)
>> imwrite(pattern,'Fig0466(b)(spatial interference pattern).tif','compression','none','resolution',300)

Figure P4.25 (Problem figure)

>>[g, S] = prob0425(400,400,2);  %See listing below.
>> imwrite(g,'FigP0425(left).tif','compression','none','resolution',300)
>> imwrite(S,'FigP0425(right).tif','compression','none','resolution',300) % Enlarged the dots in Photoshop

function [g, S] = prob0425(M, N, NPX)
%PROB0425 Images for Problem 0425.
%   [G, S] = PROB0425(M, N, NPX) Generates a image, G, of size M-by-N
%   consisting of alternating black and white vertical stripes NPX pixels
%   wide (starting with a black stripe and ending with a white one--this
%   makes an integer number of periods of a black/white pair). Image G is of
%   class double, with values 0 (black) and 1 (white).  S is the centered
%   Fourier spectrum of G.

% Generate image. (stripes.m is a DIP4E function).
g = stripes(M, N, NPX);
    
% Compute the Fourier spectrum

S = abs(fftshift(fft2(g)));

Figure 5.16  Astronaut image corrupted by sinusoidal noise. [Same as Fig. 2.45)

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0516(astronaut by moon bolder)(hi-res segment of original NASA image).tif'));
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> % generate sinusoidal noise pattern (r), its DFT (R), and its spectrum (S)
>> [r, R, S] = imnoise3(M, N, [25 25], 0.3);
>> % Noisy image.
>> g = f + r; % Save g later (see below) as .mat file (so negative values will be preserved) for posting in web site.
>> % Scale the result.
>> gs = intScaling4e(g); % g has small negative values, so scaled before writing it out.
>> % Compute the spectrum of g to show in book, so that the noise impulses can be explained.
>> G = fftshift(abs(fft2(g)));
>> Glog = intScaling4e(1 + log(G));
>> % Create notch filters. M = 1650 and N = 2000, so the center of the frequency rectangle
>> % is at (M/2) + 1 = 826 and (N/2) + 1 = 1001. Since the specified noise spike is at 
>> % (826 + 25, 1001 + 25) = (851, 1026), specify one filter at the same location. Remember that the conjugates are
>> % generated automatically.  Also, functions imnoise3 and cnotch use different conventions for specifications (they will be fixed to reconcile
>> % in the 3rd edition of DIPUM)
>> H = cnotch('ideal', 'reject', M, N, [851 1026], 2); %% Small ideal filter does much better than gaussian in this case.
>> % Center to show as image.
>> Hc = intScaling4e(fftshift(H)); % Scale for display purposes.
>> %Filter image.
>> gf = intScaling4e(dftfilt(g, H)); % gf has small negative values, so scaled before writing it out.
>> % Display results.
>> imshow(gs)
>> figure, imshow(Glog)
>> figure, imshow(Hc)
>> figure, imshow(gf) 

% Write results to disk.

 %% SAVE g as Fig0240.mat to post in Web site.  That way, positive and negative values are preserved. Make a note that g has poisitive and negative values, so when displayed without [] will not look the same as in the book.  The commnands are save('Fig0240.mat', 'g').  To get it back, type:  load Fig0240  (no single quotes needed)

>> save('Fig0240.mat', 'g')

>> imwrite(gs, 'Fig0516(a)(noisy_astronaut).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870) 
>> imwrite(Glog, 'Fig0516(b)(spectrum).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870) % Note: used Photoshop to magnified impulses
>> imwrite(Hc, 'Fig0516(c)(filter).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870)  % Filter
>> imwrite(gf, 'Fig0516(d)(filtered image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870)

Figure 5.17 Noise pattern (only) of astronaut

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0516(astronaut by moon bolder)(hi-res segment of original NASA image).tif'));
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> % generate sinusoidal noise pattern (r), its DFT (R), and its spectrum (S)
>> [r, R, S] = imnoise3(M, N, [25 25], 0.3);
>> % Noisy image.
>> g = f + r; % Save g later (see below) as .mat file (so negative values will be preserved) for posting in web site.
>> % Create notch filters. M = 1650 and N = 2000, so the center of the frequency rectangle
>> % is at (M/2) + 1 = 826 and (N/2) + 1 = 1001. Since the specified noise spike is at 
>> % (826 + 25, 1001 + 25) = (851, 1026), specify one filter at the same location. Remember that the conjugates are
>> % generated automatically.  Also, functions imnoise3 and cnotch use different conventions for specifications (they will be fixed to reconcile
>> % in the 3rd edition of DIPUM)
>> % It is now a pass notch, to pass only the data in the two locations used for rejection earlier.
>> H = cnotch('ideal', 'pass', M, N, [851 1026], 2); %% Small ideal filter does much better than gaussian in this case.
>> % Filter the corrupted image with the notchpass filter.
>> gf = intScaling4e(dftfilt(g, H)); % gf has small negative values, so scaled before writing it out.
>> figure, imshow(gf)
>> imwrite(gf, 'Fig0517(noise pattern only of corrupted astrnaute image).tif', 'compression', 'none', 'resolution', 870)

Figure 5.18 Notch filtering of Florida image.

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0518(a)(satellite_orig_noisy).tif'));
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> F = fft2(f);
>> S = intScaling4e(log10(1 + abs(fftshift(F))));
>> HR = rectrejectfilter(M, N, 25, 10, 1, 0, 5); % This is my function. Could also use recnotch from DIPUM2E.
>> g = dftfilt(f, HR);
>> % Obtain interference pattern using a bandpass filter
>> HP = 1 - HR;
>> gp = intScaling4e(dftfilt(f, HP));
>> % Spectrum times HP
>> SF = im2double(S).*fftshift(HP);
>> figure, imshow(f)
>> figure, imshow(S)
>> figure, imshow(SF)
>> figure, imshow(gp)
>> figure, imshow(g)
>> imwrite(S, 'Fig0519(b)(spectrum).tif','compression','none');
>> imwrite(SF,'Fig0519(c)(spectrum_times_filter).tif','compression','none')
>> imwrite(gp,'Fig0519(d)(interference pattern).tif','compression','none')
>> imwrite(g,'Fig0519(e)(filtered_image).tif','compression','none')

>> F = fft2(f);

>> HR = rectrejectfilter(M, N, 25, 10, 1, 0, 5); % Reject notch filter.

>> gp = intScaling4e(dftfilt(f, HP));

ac=minus1topower(a);
F=fft2(ac);

>> rpt0025=r;

%repeated for c=0.001 and c=0.00025

>> aerial_c_pt001=intScaling4e(rpt001);
>> aerial_c_pt00025=intScaling4e(rpt00025);

**************************************************************************
Figure 5.26 Blurred DIP1E Cover

>> f = im2double(imread('Fig0526(a)(original_DIP).tif'));
>> [M N] = size(f);
>> % Generate blurring filter.
>> H = motiontf(M, N, 0.1, 0.1, 1);  
>> % Get the FFT of the image. 
>> F = fft2(f);
>> % Multiply the FFT by the transfer function.
>> G = F.*H;
>> % Obtain the output image.
>> g = real(ifft2(G));
>> figure, imshow(f);
>> figure, imshow(g);

A few points to note:

1) No zero padding was used to generate the blurred image.  By not using padding, we essentially eliminated dark border effects.  This is not a problem because our "clean" blurred image could have been a much larger image that was generated with padding  and then cropped to eliminate border effects.  In other words, it really is not material whether padding was used or not, since the image is just a test pattern whose origin conceivably could be unknown.

2) The input image was not multiplied by (1)^x+y because MATLAB's fft2 function assumes that the image is not multiplied by  (1)^x+y. As a result, the filter cannot be centered either, which is the way it was generated by function "motiontf.m"  If you want to use or view the filter as a centered function, then use fftshift(H) instead.

**************************************************************************
Figure 5.27 Inverse filtering of aerial image.

THE MATLAB FUNCTIONS USED ARE FROM DIP2E


NOTE: FOR DECONVOLUTION CANNOT WORK WITH SAVED IMAGES
BECAUSE THEY HAVE LOST ACCURACY WHEN CONVERTED TO 8 BITS.  ALSO, IT'S BEST TO WORK WITH THE TRANSFORMS DIRECTLY WHEN ADDING NOISE TO AN IMAGE.  SEE COMMENTS ON THE WIENER FILTER NOTES.

 *** NEED TO POST THE BLURRED IMAGE AS MATLAB FIG SO IT CAN BE RESTORED--TIF IMAGE WON'T WORK ***

a = imread('Fig0525(a)(aerial_view_no_turb).tif');
ac = minus1topower(a);
F=fft2(ac);

H=atmosphturb(480,480,241,241,0.0025);
G=H.*F;		%G is the transform of the degraded image.

% create noise image

z = zeros(480,480);
zn=imnoise(z, gaussian',0,10^(-10));  %% Check statement in Ex 5.15 which says that the noise variance is 10^-5.  Adjust this computation to that variance if necessary so that the two match.
Gn=fft2(zn);

% form the transform of degraded image plus noise

G1=G + Gn;

Now do a straight inverse filter:

Fh1=G1./H;

f=ifft2(Fh1);
r1=abs(real(f))  %image restored with full filter.

% Start cutting off the range of values of R1.

>> co50=bwlowpass(480,480,241,241,50,10);
>> G50=co50.*Fh1;
>> g50=ifft2(G50);
>> r50=abs(real(g50));
>> imshow(r50,[])

% Got spectrum of results with 40,50,60,70 75, 85, 90
>> r1s=im2uint8(r) %%% this is the full-filtered image.
>> r40s=im2uint8(r40);
>> r70s=im2uint8(r70);
>> r85s=intScaling4e(r85);	%had to use different scaling for it to show

Wrote results out as Figs. 5.x(a), (b), (c), (d)
Used, r1s,r40s,r70s,r85

Figure 5.28 Comparison of Inverse Filtering and Wiener Filtering on Aerial Turbulence Image

[see comments in the other
wiener example].

THE MATLAB FUNCTIONS USED ARE FROM DIP2E

a = imread('Fig0525(a)(aerial_view_no_turb).tif');
ac = minus1topower(a);
F = fft2(ac);

H = atmosphturb(480,480,241,241,0.0025);
G = H.*F;		%G is the transform of the degraded image.

% create noise image

z = zeros(480,480);
zn = imnoise(z,'gaussian',0,10^(-10));
Gn = fft2(zn);

% form the transform of degraded image plus noise

G1 = G + Gn;

>> w = wiener(H,.00000001);
>> Fh1 = w.*G1;
>> f = ifft2(Fh1);
>> h1 = abs(real(f));
>> fs(h1)
>> h1s = im2uint8(h1);
>> fs(h1s)
>> 
>> imwrite(h1s,'Fig0528(c)(wiener_rest_of_noisy_turbulence).tif')
>>
